                <tr style="background-color: #FFF;"><td style="border-top:2px solid #D3D3D3; vertical-align:top; padding-bottom:4px; padding-left:5px;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:13pt"><span class="m_date">5/12/2017</span> -                 <tr id="so1" style="background-color: #FFF;"><td colspan="5" style="border-top:2px solid #D3D3D3; padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="width:100%; font-size:10pt"><center>Profiles:&nbsp;&nbsp;<a id="soa5" href="javascript:showMoreSO2013();">2013</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;<a id="soa6" href="javascript:showMoreSO2014();">2014</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;<a id="soa7" href="javascript:showMoreSO2015();">2015</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;<a id="soa8" href="javascript:showMoreSO2016();">2016</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;<a id="soa9"  href="javascript:showMoreSO2017();">2017</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;(Click Year to Expand / <a href="javascript:hideSO('so1');">Close</a>)</center></div></td></tr>
                
                
                
                <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Profile: The Mets have announced that their top two prospects, Zack Wheeler and Travis d'Arnaud will start the season at Triple-A Las Vegas. But, don't expect the battery to remain there for long. The Mets are on record saying Wheeler is more advanced then last year's upstart, Matt Harvey who made his debut July 26. Wheeler features a mid to upper 90s fastball and a wicked slider, but he's been plagued with command issues. If he remains at Las Vegas it will be to work on his command as the Flushing Faithful are too restless to permit the Front Office to penny pitch over Wheeler's super-two status. (<a href="http://bullpenbanter.com/">JD Sussman</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>A full season dominating Triple-A hitters would beneficial, but Wheeler will spend the summer honing his skills in Flushing rather than Las Vegas.  (<a href="http://bullpenbanter.com/">JD Sussman</a>)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
                <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>With Matt Harvey sidelined for 2014, all eyes around the Mets will be on Zack Wheeler. Extremely high expectations, partially set by the absurd immediate dominance of Harvey, led to Wheeler’s debut being seen as something of a disappointment. For fantasy purposes, this dynamic may help to create an opportunity for value. Wheeler finished 2013 fairly strong as still has the profile and minor league track record that predicts a very high quality major league starter. He was unable to harness the elite strikeout rate he displayed in the minors, though his 7.6 per nine was useful. Wheeler needs to hone his control and get his walks down, which will both allow him to dominate games more and last deeper in his outings. If he’s able to make incremental progress in 2014, we should see a borderline top-40 starter. It’s more realistic to think that Wheeler will give the world an enticing preview of a future ace this season than it was to expect him to replicate Harvey’s dominance right off the bat. Wheeler could become a sexy pick in the offseason, and if he does that would cut into his value. But, either way you slice it, there is true breakout potential here. (Derek Ambrosino)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Compared to the immediate dominance of Matt Harvey, some may have viewed Zack Wheeler’s debut as somewhat disappointing. However, Wheeler showed plenty to justify why many expect big things from him. There’s definite break out potential here, with borderline top-40 starter expectations this coming year, and truly elite status to follow. If the hype machine dodges Wheeler a bit this offseason, he’ll be one to target in all leagues.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
                <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>At 25 years old in 2015, Zack Wheeler could be even better. His two worst pitches -- the slider and the changeup -- still induced over 21% and 30% whiffs-per-swing respectively. While these rates are below average for these pitch-types, his fourseam, sinker and curve are all great: he had the 16th-best whiff rate on his fastball (23.14%); seventh-best whiff and 38th-best grounder rate on his sinker; and 11th-best whiff and 10th-best grounder rate on his curveball in 2014. It will take more swing-and-miss from his slider and/or changeup for him to become elite. If he had a better defense behind him, he could reach pre-2014 batting average on balls in play levels based on his contact prevention (top 25 zone-contact%) and balls in play (top 20 grounder-to-fly) outcomes. Wheeler’s expected earned run averages (3.54 SIERA and 3.49 xFIP) perfectly backed up his 3.55 ERA, and at 25, based on his repertoire, there should be more swing-and-miss to his game, which could have him approach 200 strikeouts in 33 starts. With some luck (a left on base% that approached his 2013 level) and a lower BABIP as well as additional command/development, Wheeler could turn into 3.25 ERA – 1.20 WHIP – 200 K Ace. (<a href="https://twitter.com/RotoBanter">Dan Schwartz</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Steamer is not as bullish as some, but Wheeler will only be 25 and his repertoire adds up to almost three standard deviations better than average from a swinging-strike perspective. To say that he could be the Mets’ third-best starter next year if they all stay healthy, is exciting. The New York Mets rotation commands attention.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
                <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Wheeler underwent Tommy John surgery last spring and is currently ticketed for a midseason return to the rotation. His ability to get both strikeouts and ground balls is intriguing. When he last pitched in 2014, he was one of four qualified pitchers to strike out more than a batter per inning and finish with a ground ball rate above 50% (along with Felix Hernandez, Francisco Liriano, and Clayton Kershaw -- good company). Wheeler does have flaws. His first strike rate was the worst in baseball in 2014 and he walks too many batters. Unsurprisingly, batters weren’t very willing to chase out of the zone. Wheeler hasn’t been very effective against lefties so far, likely because he’s yet to develop his changeup. He throws the pitch quite hard and by pitch type value, it was one of the worst in baseball in 2014. Wheeler’s results still haven’t matched up with the raw stuff scouts see, so there’s room for a lot of growth if he improves the command issues and changeup. That improvement may be a bit much to ask from a midseason return from Tommy John surgery, so while he’s an interesting pick this season, it’s possible he doesn’t really take the next step until 2017. (Adam McFadden)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Wheeler has huge talent and could take a few steps up the fantasy rankings if he’s able to improve his command and changeup. Just be careful not to pay for those improvements on draft day since he’s scheduled to return from Tommy John surgery midseason -- it may be overly optimistic to expect he’s able to make them this season.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
                <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Zack Wheeler enters 2017 as, most likely, the best active pitcher to have not played in the majors in two years. After undergoing Tommy John surgery in the spring of 2015, Wheeler was slated to return during the 2016 season, but he ran into setbacks during the summer and ended the year having only made one rehab start. Wheeler continues to progress, but may not be healthy by Opening Day -- and there have even been rumblings about keeping him in the bullpen for part or all of 2017. When Wheeler was last healthy in 2014, he used his 95 MPH fastball to generate both strikeouts (9.08 K/9) and grounders (54.0% GB%) in above-average numbers. Wheeler's spring training will be critical for his fantasy value; if he's pitching regularly, maintaining his velocity and showing good mechanics, he could be a risky SP4/5 with SP2/3 upside. More likely, though, you'll want to target him as a bench flier who could pay off in spades if 2017 is the year he finally makes his comeback. (Brice Russ)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Wheeler may finally make his return to the Mets this season after not having pitched in the majors since 2014. He has more upside than nearly any injured pitcher out there, but with no guarantee that he'll be healthy -- or a starter -- to start the season, he's someone to target late and thank for any value he returns.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
            </table>
        </td>

    function hideSO(a) {

        if (document.getElementById('so2') != null && a != 'so2') {

    function showMoreSO() {
        //    var panel = document.getElementById('so1');
        //    
        //    if(panel.style.display == 'none')
        //    {
        //        panel.style.display = 'inherit';
        //    }
        //    else
        //    {
        //        panel.style.display = 'inherit';
        //    }

        hideSO('so2');

        var panelo = document.getElementById('so2');

        if (panelo.style.display == 'none') {
            panelo.style.display = 'table-row';
            document.getElementById('soa2').style.fontWeight = 'bold';
        }
        else {
            panelo.style.display = 'none';
            document.getElementById('soa2').style.fontWeight = 'normal';
        }
    }

<script type="text/javascript">
    // Create the tooltips only on document load
    $(document).ready(function () {
        // Notice the use of the each() method to acquire access to each elements attributes
        $('img[tooltip]').each(function () {
            $(this).qtip({
                position: {
                    viewport: $(window),
                    at: "bottomMiddle"
                },
                content: $(this).attr('tooltip'),
                style: {
                    classes: "qtip-dark"
                }
            });
        });
    });
</script>

    function setAverage(t) {
        var elements;
        var browserCheck = (document.all) ? 1 : 0;
        if (t == '*') {
            elements = (ie) ? document.all : document.getElementsByTagName('*');
        } else {
            elements = document.getElementsByTagName(t);
        }
        for (var i = 0; i < elements.length; i++) {
            var node = elements.item(i);
            var vis = elements.item(i).style;
            for (var j = 0; j < node.attributes.length; j++) {
                if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeName == 'class') {
                    if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_average') {


                        if (browserCheck > 0) {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'block';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'block') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'block'; }
                            }

                        }

                        else {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'table-row';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'table-row') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'table-row'; }
                            }

                        }

                    }
                }
            }
        }
    }

<script type="text/javascript">
    // Create the tooltips only on document load
    $(document).ready(function () {
        // Make sure to only match links to wikipedia with a rel tag
        $('a[tipgloss]').each(function () {
            // We make use of the .each() loop to gain access to each element via the "this" keyword...
            $(this).qtip(
		{
		    content: {
		        // Set the text to an image HTML string with the correct src URL to the loading image you want to use
		        text: " ",
		        ajax: {
		            url: $(this).attr('tipgloss') // Use the rel attribute of each element for the url to load
		        }
		    },
		    position: {
		        viewport: $(window),
		        at: "top center",
		        my: "bottom center",
		        effect: false
		    },
		    show: {
		        event: "click mouseenter",
		        solo: true // Only show one tooltip at a time
		    },
		    hide: {
		        event: "click mouseleave",
		        delay: 1000,
		        fixed: true
		    },
		    style: {
		        classes: "qtip-light"
		    }
		})

            // Make sure it doesn't follow the link when we click it
        });
    });
</script>
